<div id="review_732056658" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/732056658" />
    <a title="Maria " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5769334-maria"><img alt="Maria " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600318539p2/5769334.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/732056658?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria " href="/user/show/5769334-maria">Maria </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Maria  by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/7681130-allen-grace">Allen Grace</a>
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer732056658" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16733312025905164017"><b>
  <i>Screw what Mom and Dad think. Screw the rest of the town. Screw perfection. This girl is mine.<br/><br/>		~Ryan</i>
</b><br/><br/><br/><b>REACTION AFTER READING THE BOOK</b><br/><br/>Totally happy and a little bit teary-eyed.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1382170628ra/5733205.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>*clap. clap. clap*<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380407534ra/796052.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Oh and I have a playlist for this book:</b><br/><br/><b>Ryan to Beth: </b> Kiss Me Slowly by Parachute<br/><b>Isaiah to Beth: </b> What I know by Parachute<br/><b>For Beth:</b> Broken Angel by Boyce Avenue<br/><b>Beth to Ryan:</b> Who Knew by Pink or Terrified by Katharine McPhee<br/><br/><br/>This book wasn't perfect. There were stuff here and there that made me want to th</span>
  <span id="freeText16733312025905164017" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>Screw what Mom and Dad think. Screw the rest of the town. Screw perfection. This girl is mine.<br><br>		~Ryan</i>
</b><br><br><br><b>REACTION AFTER READING THE BOOK</b><br><br>Totally happy and a little bit teary-eyed.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1382170628ra/5733205.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>*clap. clap. clap*<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380407534ra/796052.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Oh and I have a playlist for this book:</b><br><br><b>Ryan to Beth: </b> Kiss Me Slowly by Parachute<br><b>Isaiah to Beth: </b> What I know by Parachute<br><b>For Beth:</b> Broken Angel by Boyce Avenue<br><b>Beth to Ryan:</b> Who Knew by Pink or Terrified by Katharine McPhee<br><br><br>This book wasn't perfect. There were stuff here and there that made me want to throw the book out the window but I stuck with it and is totally happy that I did.<br><br><b>THE GIST</b><br><br>Beth Risk lives a life not everyone would be able to handle. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1383399827i/6538082.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>At 17, she's been through a lot and those things made her tough. It made her strong. She knew she had to be strong to protect her mother. But something happened and she got sent off to live with her uncle who used to be her favorite person in the world that is until he left her when he promised not to. <br><br>Everyone thinks Ryan Stone was perfect. He was good-looking <s>and hot</s>. He was a great pitcher. He had the perfect family. He was popular. He wasn't on the top of the class but he was smart. <br><br>But if you ask him.. He'll say...<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1383399827i/6538083.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Everyone thinks his life was perfect but what they didn't know was what was happening behind closed doors. Ryan was tired of pretending. <br><br>Because of a dare, Beth and Ryan's paths crossed. Because of a dare, their lives took a 360 degree turn. But was it for the good or the bad?<br><br><b>FIRST IMPRESSIONS</b><br><br>This would have to be my first book by Katie McGarry and I am totally hooked. Honestly, I had no intention of reading this series at all even though I've read a lot of good reviews about it. I wasn't really sure why but Allen Grace's(thanks girl!! *high five*) review made me change my mind. I was so intrigued by the guy she called Taco Bell boy.<br><br><b>THE CHARACTERS</b><br><br>I think the characters are all awesome. I liked the main ones and the secondary ones. Let me start with.<br><br><b>Beth</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382170628i/5733208.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Beth was one of those characters you'll hate but love at the same time. She was b*tchy most of the time. She had a dirty mouth. She drinks. She parties too much. She smokes weed. Eventhough she was pretty, she wasn't the type of girl you'd want to take home to meet your parents. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382170628i/5733209.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">&lt;<br><br>As you read through the book though, you'll understand why she has to be that way. You'll eventually see what her struggles are and why she has trust issues. She was the type of girl who looks tough on the outside but a real softie in the inside. What she went through in life is definitely not easy. She had to experience the harsh reality of life at a young age. She felt being unwanted by the people who should be taking care of her and not the other way around. <br><br>I kind of didn't like her at first but then who could blame her for all her insecurities and uncertainty with herself. No one was there to tell her that she was beautiful and buy her pretty dresses and give her ribbons (that she loves so much) when she was younger. Her good for nothing mother was useless. Her father was a good for nothing sperm donor who doesn't give a f*ck which was why he ran away. She has good friends though and I think they are the ones that kept her sane. That kept her moving forward. And then.. Ryan came. ^__^<br><br><b>Ryan aka Taco Bell boy</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382170628i/5733210.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>*note: i didn't intentionally picked this guy because he was shirtless. LOL*<br><br>Taco Bell boy was the reason I read this book and I was so not disappointed. I absolutely love him. He was far from the cliche-ish bad-boy-turned-good-boy male lead in most YA books. Actually, he was the good boy and he really owned up to it. <br><br>At first, I really thought he was perfect but he wasn't. He was far from perfect. He was dependent with his brother but he went away and left him which actually broke him. He felt alone with his parents who were too busy pretending that everything was perfect when it was not. He felt dependent on them too as to what he thinks he wants to do with his life. His father controlled him and he didn't even notice it.<br><br>What I loved most about Ryan was how serious he was when it comes to relationship. He was a real sweetheart. <br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <b>
    <i>"Because I love you. Beth - you're everything I want to be. You're alive and live without apology. I never would have made love to you if I thought you didn't trust me... or love me. And I never would have done it if I didn't trust and love you.</i>
  </b>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Everything with Beth started as a dare but he then called it off when he started falling for her and he wasn't scared to admit that to his friends, his schoolmates and his family *at least towards the end*. <br><br>Oh did I forget to mention that Ryan is one hell of a writer?! That even makes him more sexier. A writer with a sexy six pack abs. *I absolutely love it!*<br><br><b>Isaiah</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382170629i/5733211.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>*note: sorry about that. another shirtless guy here. LOL*<br><br>Isaiah. Well, I liked him really. He did nothing but do what is best for Beth but... I really think there was not enough chemistry with them as it is with Beth and Ryan. I haven't read the first book so I had no idea if they looked sweeter there or if Beth was different with Isaiah there but I really just thought of him as Beth's friend.. nothing more.<br><br>Sorry guys. I know a lot of you would have and have loved Isaiah but I don't like him for Beth. He doesn't bring out the best in her like Ryan can. But I do agree that he is a good friend. What I wouldn't give to have a friend like him. Sexy. Dependent. <s>HOT</s>. Cool. And a lot more. :)<br><br>I'm just so happy to hear that the next book will be about him. He does deserve a happy ending too!<br><br><b>Secondary Characters</b><br><br>I liked Noah and Echo. Although I haven't really read their story, I kind of like how supportive they are of Beth. Especially Noah. <br><br>Gwen. I hated her. She thinks she could make everything go how she wants to because she's pretty and popular. Unfortunately, that is so not true.<br><br>Uncle Scott. I liked him. He admitted he was wrong when he left and wanted to make it up to Beth. He was very admirable. <br><br>Ryan's parents. Meeh. They are crazy perfectionist it's absolutely insane.<br><br>Mark. I liked him. He wasn't afraid to go after who he really is. He didn't let his parents tell him what he is <br><br><br><b>RYAN + BETH = SWEET AND SEXY</b><br><br>This was the type of book that doesn't need to be smutty to be sexy.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1383399827i/6538084.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ryan and Beth's relationship was not insta-love. Thank goodness. They were attracted to each other physically yes but that doesn't mean they liked each other. In fact, they hated each other's guts and that is what makes their relationship work for me I guess. They got to know each other more before they fell for each other. <br><br>Makes me all dreamy about it really. LOL<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1382170629ra/5733213.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I wish I had my own Ryan that would sweep me off my feet and write me poems or stories or whatever. :D<br><br>Anyways, there were scenes where they showed how much they liked and wanted to be close to each other but nothing more than that and that's kind of refreshing. I liked that.<br><br><b>FINAL THOUGHTS</b><br><br>I liked this one and will remember Ryan and Beth for a long time. It's one of those stories that will stick to your brain and will remember and smile because it was good.<br><br>I liked Beth and Ryan's love story but what I really liked the most was the way it shows how life is never as it seems. Some things you can just see above the surface. Not everything is what it seems. Like with the case of Ryan's family. You think they have everything but they don't. Inside their house, someone was gay, someone was angry, someone was disappointed and someone felt completely alone. But if you look at their perfect family facade, you never would know, unless of course, they tell you or you are a nosy next door neighbor who likes to snoop on other people's lives. Haha.<br><br>Beth's case was different. Everyone knows what she is going through but not a lot of people were willing to help. The person she was trying to save doesn't really want to be saved and that is sh*tty. She was endangering her life for someone who doesn't give a f*ck. <br><br>Books are really a good thing. It takes you to the mind of another person and see things the way they see. It's an eye opener. And Dare You To is not just a typical YA contemporary romance with a feisty heroine and a swoon-worthy hero but it was also about life and its troubles and how they overcame it.<br><br><b>FINAL RATING</b><br><br><a href="http://media.photobucket.com/image/star%20gif/SAKORY/Gifs/1296064yv2vt9d05a.gif?o=33" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380416409ra/822333.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="http://media.photobucket.com/image/star%20gif/SAKORY/Gifs/1296064yv2vt9d05a.gif?o=33" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380416409ra/822333.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="http://media.photobucket.com/image/star%20gif/SAKORY/Gifs/1296064yv2vt9d05a.gif?o=33" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380416409ra/822333.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="http://media.photobucket.com/image/star%20gif/SAKORY/Gifs/1296064yv2vt9d05a.gif?o=33" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380416409ra/822333.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="http://media.photobucket.com/image/star%20gif/SAKORY/Gifs/1296064yv2vt9d05a.gif?o=33" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380416409ra/822333.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

    <a title="littlebookbosomed bookreview" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6285960-littlebookbosomed-bookreview"><img alt="littlebookbosomed bookreview" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494656862p2/6285960.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/421695763?book_show_action=true">Sep 25, 2012</a>

<div id="review_499796108" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/499796108" />
    <a title="Giselle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle"><img alt="Giselle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310159877p2/4800103.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/499796108?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Giselle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Giselle" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle">Giselle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=signed">signed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer499796108" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14926380343137442713">After Pushing the Limits became one of my favorite reads of last year, I went into this one with a lot of enthusiasm and high expectations. I'm sad that I didn't en up loving it as much, but I still quite enjoyed it and am happy that I read it. I also can see why so many are enamored by it, if I had read it at another time I might have enjoyed it much more as well. As it stands I've been reading a string of similarly plotted books lately so my patience for certain elements of the book has been w</span>
  <span id="freeText14926380343137442713" style="display:none">After Pushing the Limits became one of my favorite reads of last year, I went into this one with a lot of enthusiasm and high expectations. I'm sad that I didn't en up loving it as much, but I still quite enjoyed it and am happy that I read it. I also can see why so many are enamored by it, if I had read it at another time I might have enjoyed it much more as well. As it stands I've been reading a string of similarly plotted books lately so my patience for certain elements of the book has been worn thin.<br><br>Unlike with Pushing the Limits, I had a difficult time with the characters and romance in this sequel. I liked the characters okay, and the chemistry is definitely not missing between them, but the back and forth, hot and cold romance they develop went on a little too long for me until I became utterly exhausted with it. Beth is dealing with a drunk mother who has an abusive boyfriend, making her somewhat of a bitter person who blocks everyone out. She has a hard time opening up to anybody, let alone letting anyone get close enough for her to fall in love. Consequently, she's not an easy character to like, but she's meant to be that way. We're meant to sympathize with her situation, which I did, and like how she grows out of it through the story (like expected), but this did not happen until after she had me wanting to rip my hair out. The problem was more with how she dealt with Ryan than anything else. Athletic superstar, popular, rich, and with a bright future ahead of him, Ryan is Beth's polar opposite. It's, at the same time, the allure and the downfall of the romance. Beth being so cautious makes it extremely difficult for Ryan to get her to let him in. At first this was a great kind of frustration. The kind where you yearn for them to finally open up to each other and become rocks to lean on, however this fails to happen for what felt like an extremely long time, I began to lose my eagerness and gain some irritation. My patience for Beth to finally get a clue that the whole world wasn't out to get her ran out and I simply wanted to slap her silly for trying to ruin every good thing she had. I get that she's had a very <i>very</i> hard life, her crappy attitude was just making it worse for herself which made it hard for me to connect with her more than on the surface. Perhaps her keeping everyone at arm's length worked TOO well :) I also can't fail to mention the constant referral to Ryan's looks. She must have described his gorgeous godliness over a dozen times in the book. We get it, he's sculpted perfection, let's move on, shall we?<br><br>No matter my complaints, the characters are still carved into real human beings. The character development doesn't miss its mark as Katie, again, creates realistic characters with hearts you can feel beating and breaking. Even though I was a little irritated, I still couldn't help but feel sympathetic towards both of them. Beth for her screwed up upbringing, and Ryan for the pressure he was brought up under. Another part of these books that I enjoy is how it's not JUST about the romance. Beth has to acclimate to a whole new life where she feels anything but welcome, while Ryan is looking at his family crumbling after his brother announced he was gay to a father who thinks the most important thing is perfect outward appearance. <br><br>As with any companion novel it's always fun to see old characters again. While I loved hearing from Echo and Noah in their brief cameos in this book, Isaiah stole my heart away. I love his character and my heart broke for him in more ways than one. His character has just as much soul and presence, getting his story line ready for the next book. The 3rd installment of this series will be his story, and I absolutely cannot wait for it as I have a very big feeling it will be my absolute favorite. I just hope he gets his happy ending or I may be found in a puddle of my own tears. <br><br>Dare You To may not have been as good to me as I had hoped, but I still found myself flipping the pages eagerly, waiting and hoping these two will finally give in to each other completely. The love and chemistry they share make all the hurt and frustration worth it. <br><br>--<br><i>An advance copy was provided by the publisher for review.</i><br><br>For more of my reviews, visit my blog at <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Xpresso Reads</a> <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380236618i/681468.png" width="380" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14926380343137442713" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_410607741" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/410607741" />
    <a title="Jennifer Kyle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9916227-jennifer-kyle"><img alt="Jennifer Kyle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514915429p2/9916227.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/410607741?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer Kyle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer Kyle" href="/user/show/9916227-jennifer-kyle">Jennifer Kyle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17372887-dare-you-to">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9916227-jennifer-kyle?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer410607741" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17411580622684650680"><b>
  <i>"Game on, Skater Girl. Game On."</i>
</b><br/><br/>Katie McGarry’s <b>Dare You To</b> is YA at its best!! <br/><br/>I was thoroughly engrossed in this story from the first page and I have to admit that I read it straight through and I still wanted more. There isn't a cliffhanger and we get an hea, I just could have read about these characters forever. Luckily Katie McGarry will have another installment to this series.<br/><br/>The story is told in alternating povs of Beth Risk and Ryan Stone. <br/><br/>Who’s Ryan you ask? This is Ryan...<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380390622i/752434._SY540_.jpg' width='300' height='360' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>Ryan is </span>
  <span id="freeText17411580622684650680" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>"Game on, Skater Girl. Game On."</i>
</b><br><br>Katie McGarry’s <b>Dare You To</b> is YA at its best!! <br><br>I was thoroughly engrossed in this story from the first page and I have to admit that I read it straight through and I still wanted more. There isn't a cliffhanger and we get an hea, I just could have read about these characters forever. Luckily Katie McGarry will have another installment to this series.<br><br>The story is told in alternating povs of Beth Risk and Ryan Stone. <br><br>Who’s Ryan you ask? This is Ryan...<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380390622i/752434._SY540_.jpg" width="300" height="360" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Ryan is beautiful inside and out. He is charming, talented baseball pitcher, virgin, high school senior, popular and completely swoon worthy. I loved this guy!<br><br>Ryan and his buddies are constantly playing games of dare with each other. The dares are usually silly and harmless in nature. When Ryan is dared to get (a) name and (b)phone number of a girl who walks in Taco Bell his life will never be the same. <br> <br>The skater girl was none other than Beth Risk. Beth is the best friend of Isaiah and Noah from Pushing the Limits. A reader remembers Beth as the foul mouth, foul attitude girl, but there is so much more to her. Beth’s determination to save her mother from herself is more than heroic. The beautiful little girl with ribbons is still in there and I truly connected with her.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777606i/369874.jpg" width="290" height="260" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Beth finds herself in a big mess…<br><br>Cue in Uncle Scott. He was a fantastic character!! He steps in to rescue Beth and give her a new life. There are several stipulations to his help but all are done out of love. <br> <br>As the story unfolds it appears that her new home with Uncle Scott lands her starting a new high school where none other than Ryan Stone attends. Also, her childhood best friend Lacy who attends the school reconnects with her, another terrific character.<br><br>While Beth and Ryan move past the dare and find something so special in each other. Beth learns to trust and lay down roots and these two fall in love. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380390622i/752435._SY540_.jpg" width="300" height="360" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>
  <i> "I told you I loved you in this rain and when you doubt my words, I want you to look at this bottle.”</i>
</b><br><br>Ryan’s life isn’t perfect he struggles with his brother’s absence as well as whether to go straight to professional baseball or college. He wasn’t expecting love like he found with Beth and he never faltered in telling and showing her. <br><br><b>
  <i>“I won't let you go." I blink. As if he could stop me. "You won't let me go." "No, I won't let you go. You're mine and I don't lose.”</i>
</b><br><br>Isaiah, Isaiah, my heart broke for him. I can't wait for his book.<br><br>I could go on and on about this story. I just loved it! If you liked a good YA book with a hea then Dare You To will be released on <b>May 28, 2013</b> enjoy!<br><br>*ARC kindly provided by Harlequin Limited via Netgalley in exchange of an honest review</span>

<div id="review_361199261" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/361199261" />
    <a title="Ari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3564852-ari"><img alt="Ari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451393828p2/3564852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/361199261?book_show_action=true">Jul 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ari" href="/user/show/3564852-ari">Ari</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=arc-galley-or-author">arc-galley-or-author</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer361199261" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9734929787102741544"><a href='http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/katie-mcgarry/review-dare-you-to.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380382837i/740894.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>From time to time I like to read love stories.<br/>I like to read stories that make me smile, stories about first love and hope and innocence. I like to read stories about opposite people, from very different backgrounds, that discover that there is something that can bind their worlds.<br/><br/>From time to time I like to forget about work and day to day duties, and instead curl up in my bed with a cup of tea and a cute book that can make giggle and sigh and keep my fingers crossed for a happy ending..<br/><br/>Whe</span>
  <span id="freeText9734929787102741544" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/katie-mcgarry/review-dare-you-to.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380382837i/740894.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>From time to time I like to read love stories.<br>I like to read stories that make me smile, stories about first love and hope and innocence. I like to read stories about opposite people, from very different backgrounds, that discover that there is something that can bind their worlds.<br><br>From time to time I like to forget about work and day to day duties, and instead curl up in my bed with a cup of tea and a cute book that can make giggle and sigh and keep my fingers crossed for a happy ending..<br><br>When I started reading "Dare you to" I had 2 things on my mind:<br><br>1. How much I loved "Pushing The Limits", the first book in the series;<br>2. How much I remembered <em>not</em> liking Beth.<br><br>You see, intentional or not, you always get to compare (at least a tiny bit) the books in a series. This is why I was happy to see that this story was even better than the first one. Also, I was happy to see how <em>likeable</em> Beth can really be when you get to know her better.<br><br>She has had a tough life, that's why she kept a thick shield protecting her from everything and everyone around. Her heart has been broken too many times to count, on too many levels, so she didn't want anyone close to her - and when someone finally got under her skin, she knew how to push that person away in a blink of an eye.<br><br>I understood her need to trick Ryan into taking her to see her mother, her need to protect the woman that was never there for her (do I really need to tell you how much I loathed that woman?). I understood why she didn't trust Ryan that much and why it seemed impossible to believe that he might like her. I understood her anger against the whole damn world, I understood why she did confuse friendship with love for a while, I understood why she needed someone so different to save her from her own misery.<br><blockquote>“You're a lot like that bird in the barn. You're so scared that you're going to be caged in forever you can't see the way out. You smack yourself against the wall again and again and again. The door is open, Beth. Stop running in circles and walk out.”</blockquote><br>We are made to think that good guys are boring.<br>All that book-marketing advertises is bad boys in leather jackets that treat girls awfully. They throw them in our faces until we forget that there is something else that we need: someone that cares, someone to treat us right, someone to tell us beautiful things, someone to make us laugh, someone to really "get" us, to understand us like no one else, someone to make our hearts flutter with just a smile or a soft touch.<br><br>Maybe this is another reason I loved this book so much, because it proves that a 'good' guy can be such a cutie. I mean who needs bad boys when you have someone like Ryan, right? I hate making comparisons but this is what I expected from <a title="Review: Chain Reaction" href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/simone-elkeles/chain-reaction-review.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Chain Reaction</a> a year ago. I wanted a bad girl with troubled past and a good boy to be turned bad. I wanted sparkles and hotness, and realistic conversations and less love at first sight and more of the couple getting to know each other, to care for each other.. I wanted to fall in love with them too. And here I <em>did</em>.<br><br>Also, I remember in "<a title="Review: Pushing The Limits" href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/katie-mcgarry/review-pushing-the-limits.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Pushing The Limits</a>" how I liked Noah and how I've been so touched by his story and his need to take care of his siblings, but his love-interest, Echo, was a whole different story. She gave me headaches because she didn't have much of a backbone.<br><br>But in "Dare You To" somehow I managed to like both Ryan and Beth as different as they were and as impossible as Beth can be sometimes. Yes, it's not like she is perfect (she's had her share of bad decisions and sometimes I didn't approve of her reactions and I wanted to knock some sense into her) but for me Beth was a better character, so much more realistically portrayed.<br><br>And Ryan, he was a real sweetheart!<br><br>And together they were so cute and fun to be around (or <em>in their minds</em>). Seriously, they had me laughing all the time with their teasing and their dares and I think that they are absolutely perfect for each other.<br><blockquote> "I told you I loved you in this rain and when you doubt my words, I want you to look at this bottle.”</blockquote><br>I know. I loved Isaiah and it broke my heart to see Beth break <i>his</i> heart, but how could she <em>not</em>? You don't decide who you love, the feeling just creeps into your soul and you can only follow its lead. But don't worry, I hear that Isaiah is going to get his own girl (maybe a good girl), and I can't wait to see his own story unfold.<br><br>Now that we're near the bottom of the review I assume that you want to know what to expect from this book, right? Well, there will be some pretty funny scenes, some emotional moments, quite some romance, a bit of suspense here and there and a big dose of awesome!<br>So what I mean is that..  I dare you to pick up this book and read it!<br>Or not really, because if you liked the first book in the series you will probably really-really want to get your hands on this one when it becomes available.<br><br>Happy midnight reading!<br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/katie-mcgarry/review-dare-you-to.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380334106i/693595.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i> * This review can also be found at <a title="ReadingAfterMidnight" href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/katie-mcgarry/review-dare-you-to.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">ReadingAfterMidnight.com</a> </i><br><br>Book Source: ARC kindly provided by the publisher for review. I can never thank them enough!<br>PS: I still think that the guy in the cover looks kinda Ken-alike (and yes, that still creeps me out a bit)<br>____________________________________________<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (EN)</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/readingaftermidnight" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/lil_aree" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://readingaftermidnight.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> |<a href="http://www.bloglovin.com/en/blog/3285482/reading-after-midnight/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Bloglovin'</a> | <a href="http://ro.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (RO)</a><br>____________________________________________<br><br>First thoughts:<br><i>4.5 stars and I might decide to round it to 5. <br>I liked it more compared to the first book - the storyline was a bit more fluid and I liked the characters a lot more. <br>PS: the guy on the cover creeps me out, he is so... Ken-alike o.O</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="9734929787102741544" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_423892211" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/423892211" />
    <a title="Sandra " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9752625-sandra"><img alt="Sandra " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1345749155p2/9752625.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/423892211?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sandra " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sandra " href="/user/show/9752625-sandra">Sandra </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9752625-sandra?shelf=liked-the-characters-some-or-all">liked-the-characters-some-or-all</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9752625-sandra?shelf=omfg">omfg</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9752625-sandra?shelf=rolling-my-eyes">rolling-my-eyes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9752625-sandra?shelf=sexy-males">sexy-males</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9752625-sandra?shelf=love-triangles">love-triangles</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9752625-sandra?shelf=melting-inside-awwww">melting-inside-awwww</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9752625-sandra?shelf=reviewed-books">reviewed-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9752625-sandra?shelf=sad">sad</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer423892211" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6144938212476716247"><b>4.5 STARS TO A HEART-POUNDING READ!!!</b><br/><br/><i>Dare You To</i> is a companion novel to <i>Pushing The Limits</i>, which i really enjoyed. I think this was a tiny bit better and i loved it. At times i couldn't put it down!<br/><br/><a href='http://postimage.org/' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380392689i/755989.jpg' alt='47c5642a 5742 40db 96e0 762cbfa05dbb zps140c7840' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a target='_blank' href='http://postimage.org/' rel='nofollow noopener'></a><br/><br/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>Isaiah is my safe. He has always been. He's that place where i fall when the world turns into chaos. </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Isaiah is Beth's Risk only true friend that she trusts with her life. He know her secrets. He knows her mother is an addict and alcoholic living with an abusive asshole of a boyfriend, and th</span>
  <span id="freeText6144938212476716247" style="display:none"><b>4.5 STARS TO A HEART-POUNDING READ!!!</b><br><br><i>Dare You To</i> is a companion novel to <i>Pushing The Limits</i>, which i really enjoyed. I think this was a tiny bit better and i loved it. At times i couldn't put it down!<br><br><a href="http://postimage.org/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380392689i/755989.jpg" alt="47c5642a 5742 40db 96e0 762cbfa05dbb zps140c7840" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a target="_blank" href="http://postimage.org/" rel="nofollow noopener"></a><br><br><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>Isaiah is my safe. He has always been. He's that place where i fall when the world turns into chaos. </b>
</blockquote><br><br>Isaiah is Beth's Risk only true friend that she trusts with her life. He know her secrets. He knows her mother is an addict and alcoholic living with an abusive asshole of a boyfriend, and that Beth is the only one who takes care of her. <br><br>But when a lie and cover up leaves Beth in jail, her long lost uncle shows up and takes custody of her. Beth has no choice but to live with her uncle and is struggling to start fresh. <br><br><b>In enter...</b><br><br><a href="http://postimage.org/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380392689i/755990.jpg" alt="cabaaefb d1a1 4d5f a7d7 371f938d63d3 zpsd289cc18" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a target="_blank" href="http://postimage.org/app.php" rel="nofollow noopener"></a><br><br><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"You should laugh more," he says.<br>I swallow. "Life hasn't given me much to laugh about."<br>"I could change that." Ryan invaded my personal space and every part of him connect with a part of me.</b>
</blockquote><br><br>Ryan Stone is the schools most popular, gorgeous golden boy. With secrets he isn't willing to share and holds inside. When he get's dared to get Beth's phone number and then go out with her on a date in public, he knows one thing - he doesn't like loosing and he will not fail. <br><br>But Ryan get's to know Beth better, and he sees that she's more than dark hair and bad attitude. Soon what started as a dare becomes so much more, but can Ryan protect Beth from the past that is coming back to haunt her?? Will he show her that his feelings are true and gain her trust?<br><br><br><b>WILL THEY LET EACH OTHER IN?</b><br><br><a href="http://postimage.org/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380392689i/755991.jpg" alt="wpid its ok to cry3" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a target="_blank" href="http://postimage.org/" rel="nofollow noopener"></a><br><br><br><br>As i said before, i think this is better from <i>Pushing The Limits</i>, mainly because the ending didn't confuse the heck out of me and i felt a deeper connection to the characters. <br><br><b>Beth</b> was my fav character, i felt a deep connection with her and understanding! Now, i read in some reviews that readers did not like her. Some said she was rude and just unlikable. <br><br><a href="http://postimage.org/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380392689ra/755992.gif" alt="tumblr lwg6cwa Mz A1qzjix8" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a target="_blank" href="http://postimage.org/app.php" rel="nofollow noopener"></a><br><br><br><br>OK, i'm not disagreeing with her being a bitch. But seriously people? Seriously? What did you expect from a 17 year old girl who has been through so many sh*t in life? To be all angelic and smiles? I hate to break it to ya, but that's how most teens are, OK? And Beth not only has a reason, but <b>reasons</b>, and actually has the right to being the way she is. <br><br><a href="http://postimage.org/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380392689ra/755993.gif" alt="Oprah umad" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a target="_blank" href="http://postimage.org/app.php" rel="nofollow noopener"></a><br><br><br><br><b>Ryan</b> was a likable character and most of the time i loved him, especially towards the end. But sometimes i was annoyed with him for being such a coward, for not manning up to stand up to his farther and say "You know what? Screw.You. I will do what i like and you have no say in how i live my life." I was proud of him, however, when he did just that. <br><br><a href="http://postimage.org/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380392689ra/755994.gif" alt="802" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a target="_blank" href="http://postimage.org/app.php" rel="nofollow noopener"></a><br><br><br><br><b>Overall</b>, <i>Dare You To</i> is a fab and <b>heart-wrenching</b> read that i loved. I'm looking forwards to readig Isaiah's story when it comes out (next year??). It was a <b>bit too full of drama</b> for my liking but i didn't mind much.I extremely enjoyed reading about Beth's problems and life, and recommend this book especially to <b>Contemporary Romance lovers.<br><br>Thanks Vibha for BR with me. It was fun darling!!</b> <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="6144938212476716247" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText11582895012962032958" style="display:none"><br />It’s a lot like the first book where even though both of the characters have a lot of baggage, one obvious, one not, the story still managed to entertain me as a reader. The sports element is also very interesting and I liked that the jock is also an excellent writer at the same time. I also appreciate the pairing up of the couple with completely opposite personalities and even opposite worlds and how they were able to complement each other. </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/437590548?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer437590548" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12150281898470597294"><b>SALE $1.99 ➜ <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://amzn.to/1hwhnV5'>http://amzn.to/1hwhnV5</a> </b><br/>6/8/2014<br/>**************<br/><br/><b>****4 'Ribbons of Hope' Stars**** </b><br/><br/> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380394836i/760332._SX540_.png' width='340' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This is the <i>love story</i> of <b>Ryan & Beth</b> told in both points of view.<br/><br/><b> Ryan</b> is a high school baseball star. His friends and him are into daring each other to do stuff.<br/><br/>We meet, <b>Beth</b>, in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10194514.Pushing_the_Limits__Pushing_the_Limits___1_' title='Pushing the Limits (Pushing the Limits, #1) by Katie McGarry' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pushing the Limits</a>. I didn't care for her in that book but by the end of this book she grew on me. <br/><br/>One simple dare leads to Ryan trying to gain Beth's phone number at a Taco Bell. Beth's answer to Ryan is written on the palm o</span>

<div id="review_507691286" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/507691286" />
    <a title="Ash Wednesday" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10484016-ash-wednesday"><img alt="Ash Wednesday" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379043440p2/10484016.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/507691286?book_show_action=true">Jan 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ash Wednesday" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ash Wednesday" href="/user/show/10484016-ash-wednesday">Ash Wednesday</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Readers who enjoyed Hopeless... which basically covers everyone I know</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=review">review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=cliches">cliches</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=smart-hero">smart-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=sporty-spice">sporty-spice</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer507691286" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6981411998257362047"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380405343i/789438.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>
  <i>4 STARS</i>
</b><br/><br/>I wasn't the biggest fan of Noah and Echo's book, mostly because I felt it was bogged down by the heaviness of the theme without succeeding at making me actually care for the characters (especially Echo) enough to sympathize. I didn't even care much for Beth and was certainly not raring to know her story. She came across as a whiny, pessimistic, emo, wannabe.<br/><br/>So this was a pleasant curve ball for me.<br/><br/>This is a girl book. You know, the kind that your boyfriend will never admit to his fri</span>
  <span id="freeText6981411998257362047" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380405343i/789438.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>4 STARS</i>
</b><br><br>I wasn't the biggest fan of Noah and Echo's book, mostly because I felt it was bogged down by the heaviness of the theme without succeeding at making me actually care for the characters (especially Echo) enough to sympathize. I didn't even care much for Beth and was certainly not raring to know her story. She came across as a whiny, pessimistic, emo, wannabe.<br><br>So this was a pleasant curve ball for me.<br><br>This is a girl book. You know, the kind that your boyfriend will never admit to his friends he's read it (because you forced him to) but will probably stash a paperback copy of under the bed. And because this is that kind of book…<br><br><b>
  <i>Fearless forecast #13: Once released, this book is going to set my GR feed to a perpetual lag with all the gushing and the squeeing and the sniffling and the #ohmygodRyans. </i>
</b><br><br>Because that's exactly what I did in the closeted silence of my heart (I'm a closet squee-er).<br><br>The key to enjoying this book is to reading it like you're watching a John Hughes movie: don't resist the charm. There's no shame in being charmed by a strong heroine and a sweet hero dancing around each other under the premise of a dare. There's nothing wrong with smiling and clutching your heart over a bottle-full of rain. And it's perfectly alright to have that scratchy feeling in your throat while watching the hero save the heroine from her ghastly past.<br><br>Because make no mistake about it, this is a YA-CR formula story. You won't see anything new and cliches will be all over the place. But when executed and written well enough, there can never be enough teen movie grief or homecoming party drama or dysfunctional families that can make me quit this cliche.<br><br>This was written in alternating POVs of Ryan and Beth and yet it still managed to pull off character complexity and, more importantly, excellent consistency. Whenever I come back to reading this after setting it aside for a while, it wasn't hard to be immersed again and pick up where I left off my sympathy for the characters.<br><br>While it is a teeny-bop love story, I was glad to see it deal at depth with Ryan and Beth's issues outside of each other. More than anything, the story explored how hard it is to accept that you may be more than who you believe yourself to be. <br><br>Ryan is standing on a precipice: he has the world at his feet but he doesn't know what to do with it. His conflict stems from what he wants and what everybody else wants from him. Because EVERYONE wants something from him (i.e. his parents, his friends, his teammates, his English teacher) and he's too much of a winner to let anyone down. There's an innocent kindness and inherent honor in his character that makes him instantly likable. Of course the fact that he's a hot baseball player helps. <br><br>Baseball. Yawn.<br><br>Sorry, but what got me all a-tittering was that he's also a literary genius who writes and dedicates a zombie love story to Beth. If any series needs a novella, this is it. I want to know what happens to George the zombie and Olivia, dammit.<br><br>On the other hand, nobody wants to have anything to do with Beth. She's an archive of neglect and the failures of her parents, Scott, her friends (Noah and Isaiah)… everyone has left her at some point to fend for herself. Which she does to the best of her abilities. It's tricky to make a strong, angst-ridden heroine likable (too much makes her a b*tch, too little makes her pretentious) but she's made a fan out of me in 300-something pages. It's very hard to belittle her pain and the way she reacts to everyone makes complete and utter sense without making it embarrassing for me to root for her.<br><br>Outside the predictable plot and formulaic, cookie-cutter characters, I have very little to complain about. I would've liked a bit more time between Beth and Scott and maybe temper down the drama a little towards the last 25% but these were very small issues I had. If anything, I was having a hard time looking for the misses in this one.<br><br>Overall, a better and stronger sophomore effort from Katie McGarry. One that has made a fan out of this closet squee-er.<br><br><i>ARC provided by Harlequin Teen thru Netgalley in exchange for an honest review</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="6981411998257362047" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Sofia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5927169-sofia"><img alt="Sofia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1496236285p2/5927169.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/396198853?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sofia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sofia" href="/user/show/5927169-sofia">Sofia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer396198853" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17267642006987619951"><b>"There are memories that exist in my mind that are so clear that if I focus on them enough I could practically relive them"</b> -Beth<br/><br/><u>Warning</u>:Before starting the book make sure you have a box of tissues lying besides you.<br/><br/>When I finished <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10194514.Pushing_the_Limits__Pushing_the_Limits___1_' title='Pushing the Limits (Pushing the Limits, #1) by Katie McGarry' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pushing the Limits</a> and saw that Beth is getting her own story I was beyond surprised to see that Beth isn't getting with Isaiah but someone else!!!I loved Isaiah as much as I loved Noah!!!What a pity!I really wanted to see them together..<br/><br/>Now that I have finished <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13561164.Dare_You_To__Pushing_the_Limits___2_' title='Dare You To (Pushing the Limits, #2) by Katie McGarry' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dare </a></span>
  <span id="freeText17267642006987619951" style="display:none"><b>"There are memories that exist in my mind that are so clear that if I focus on them enough I could practically relive them"</b> -Beth<br /><br /><u>Warning</u>:Before starting the book make sure you have a box of tissues lying besides you.<br /><br />When I finished <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10194514.Pushing_the_Limits__Pushing_the_Limits___1_" title="Pushing the Limits (Pushing the Limits, #1) by Katie McGarry" rel="nofollow noopener">Pushing the Limits</a> and saw that Beth is getting her own story I was beyond surprised to see that Beth isn't getting with Isaiah but someone else!!!I loved Isaiah as much as I loved Noah!!!What a pity!I really wanted to see them together..<br /><br />Now that I have finished <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13561164.Dare_You_To__Pushing_the_Limits___2_" title="Dare You To (Pushing the Limits, #2) by Katie McGarry" rel="nofollow noopener">Dare You To</a> I can only say that I couldn't have been more wrong. Although Beth and Isaiah were a nice combination,Beth and Ryan rocked.They chalenged each other,they learned things from each other and they finally discovered what love really is.The main idea of the book was how hard it's for some people to trust others.And for Beth,it was really hard.No one knows better than her what abandonment and betrayal is.<br /><br />Ryan came into her life when Beth needed him the most.Although they both thought differently,for me they were prefect.Ok,they had major family problems.But who hasn't ???<br /><br />However,they were times that I did not approve of Beth's actions.Scott, her uncle, gave her the opportunity to live a new life but she didn't take it even when Isaiah and Noah insisted that she does.I'm just glad Ryan convinced her to give him a chance.<br /><br />As far as Isaiah is concerned, I was so sorry for him.He was so caring,protective and he loved Beth so much.But,I think that Beth was right when she told him that what they share isn't love.<br /><br />Overall,the book was AMAZING.It was so emotional at times that it had me crying and there were other times that I couldn't stop laughing.Also ,there were some scenes that both Noah and Echo were present.I really enjoyed those scenes.There was even a particular scene in which, almost all the characters were present.Here's a taste: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">["<br /><br />Noah "Stare any longer,Ryan, and I'll kick you ass"<br />Echo "Noah.Don't."<br />Beth "What did I say about staring?"<br />Ryan "I apologize"<br />Echo "See?Manners."<br />(the scene takes place in a party that Beth takes Ryan and where Ryan meets Echo for the first time)  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I absolutely recommend this book and I'm looking forward to reading the next book in the series,<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17233800.Crash_Into_You__Pushing_the_Limits___3_" title="Crash Into You (Pushing the Limits, #3) by Katie McGarry" rel="nofollow noopener">Crash Into You</a>,Isaiah's book(so happy he will get his happy ever after).<br /><br />*ARC provided by NetGalley<br /><br />First posted on: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://sofialovesreading.blogspot.gr/2013/02/dare-you-to-by-katie-mcgarry.html">http://sofialovesreading.blogspot.gr/...</a></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer590451708" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer313013063755641097"><b>4 stars! Katie McGarry sure has teenage angst down pat!</b><br/><br/>I really liked this book despite a few issues that I had with it. For the first few chapters I felt a bit annoyed- I mean, come on! You know we were dying for Beth and Isaiah to have their happy ending! Poor Isaiah... I spent a good amount of time mourning my preconceived notion that this book would be about Beth and Isaiah. Then, I was going to slap Katie McGarry for pulling a "She's All That" plot twist... if this whole book was going to b</span>
  <span id="freeText313013063755641097" style="display:none"><b>4 stars! Katie McGarry sure has teenage angst down pat!</b><br /><br />I really liked this book despite a few issues that I had with it. For the first few chapters I felt a bit annoyed- I mean, come on! You know we were dying for Beth and Isaiah to have their happy ending! Poor Isaiah... I spent a good amount of time mourning my preconceived notion that this book would be about Beth and Isaiah. Then, I was going to slap Katie McGarry for pulling a "She's All That" plot twist... if this whole book was going to be about a dare followed by Beth finding out about the dare and getting pissed at the end... well, then I was OUT. Thankfully, Ms. McGarry is smarter than that. The book really grew on me.<br /><br />One of my favorite things was that this book was a twist on the "virginal girl and bad boy" trope. A bad girl and an innocent guy- YES PLEASE! I loved that element of the book. It was really nice to see. I actually would have preferred if Katie McGarry went all out and made Beth <i>really</i> experienced. If she had made Beth a sex-positive teen, I think it would have been more gutsy. She didn't necessarily have to have had to sleep with lots of guys, but having Beth be more confident with her sexuality would have been a bolder move. But maybe that is just me... <br /><br />I had some issues with most of the adults in this book. Allison was just a horrible person- I don't think she redeems herself at all. She doesn't want to know about Scott's past and rougher side: That isn't how someone who loves someone acts. I also think Ryan's parents were disgusting bigots. I felt no sympathy for either of them. And Beth's mom... just horrible. But I sympathized with Beth a little on that. It is hard to abandon the person who is supposed to love you and shred your last hope of any sense of familial normalcy. <br /><br />My heart broke for Isaiah all during this book. I felt his gut-wrenching pain over losing Beth and her inability to love him as he deserves to be loved. I hope Isaiah gets his own book next- he deserves it. <br /><br />Overall, I think this book did a great job of captivating me. I stayed up very late to finish it, which certainly says something about my enjoyment level. I am very impressed with Katie McGarry thus far and can't wait to read what she comes up with next. <br /><br />**Copy provided by the publisher in exchange for an honest review**</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('549yRUPQhOCcFyfU0S3Gaa3WQwfjr21FWO125+bNThHdqRuX+I5NiDs8k7Um2My2e4mkzy0i4yIDkzBWK468iw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('dsb8keR2FN9uTtgAd+HJyyMkSXx9pomtfQ4vWKKssNJM4JVDXyjdt8llbGGAFMMU9XuutLMrB8omcGnpb+9CSA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>
